A poet says, [using a phrase from which this application of the verb probably originated,] <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">بَاضَ النَّعَامُ بِهِ فَنَفَّرَ أَهْلَهُ</foreign>

                  </quote> (IAar,) i. e. <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نعام</foreign>, meaning the <foreign lang="ar">نَعَائِم</foreign>, [or Twentieth Mansion of the Moon,] <hi rend="ital">sent down rain upon it, and so put to flight its occupants, except him who remained incurring the risk of</hi> dying from <hi rend="ital">disease, wasting away:</hi> [the last word being in the gen. case, by poetic license, because the next before it is in that case; like <foreign lang="ar">خَرِبٍ</foreign> in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا جُحْرُ ضَبٍّ خَرِبٍ</foreign>:] the poet is describing a valley rained upon and in consequence producing herbage; for the rain of the asterism called <foreign lang="ar">النعائم</foreign> is in the hot season, [when that asterism sets aurorally, (see <foreign lang="ar">مَنَازِلُ القَمَرِ</foreign>, in art. <foreign lang="ar">نزل</foreign>,)] whereupon there grows, at the roots of the <foreign lang="ar">حَلِىّ</foreign>, a plant called <foreign lang="ar">نَشْر</foreign>, which is poisonous, killing beasts that eat of it: the verse is explained as above by El-Mohellebee: (IB:) or, as IAar says, the poet means rain that falls at the <foreign lang="ar">نَوْء</foreign> [by which we are here to understand the setting aurorally] of <foreign lang="ar">النعائم</foreign>; and that when this rain falls, the wise flees and the stupid remains. (O.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">بَاضَ بِالمَكَانِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He remained, stayed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode, in the place</hi> [like as a bird does in the place where she lays her eggs].                   <hi rend="ital">An egg</hi> (Msb) of an ostrich, (Mgh,) and of any bird, (S, Mgh, Msb, K,) and the like, i. e. of anything that is termed <foreign lang="ar">صَمُوخٌ</foreign> [or having merely an ear-hole] as distinguished from such as is termed <foreign lang="ar">أَذُونٌ</foreign> [or having an ear that is called <foreign lang="ar">أُذُنٌ</foreign>]: so called because of its whiteness: (TA:) n. un. of   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3630-1" target="بَيْضٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n3629"/></foreign>: (S, M, * Msb, K:) pl. [of the former] <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَاتٌ</foreign> (M, Sgh, K) and <foreign lang="ar">بَيَضَاتٌ</foreign>, which latter is irreg., (M, Sgh,) and only used by poetic license; (Sgh;) and (of <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضٌ</foreign>, M) <foreign lang="ar">بُيُوضٌ</foreign>. (M, K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">أَفْرَخَتِ البَيْضَةُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The egg had in it a young bird.</hi> (ISh.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَفْرَخَ بَيْضَةُ القَوْمِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">What was hidden, of the affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">case, of the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">company of men, became apparent.</hi> (ISh.) [See also art. <foreign lang="ar">فرخ</foreign>.] <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَةُ البَلَدِ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">The egg which the ostrich abandons.</hi> (S, M, K.) And hence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ أَذَلُّ مِنْ بَيْضَةِ البَلَدِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He is more abject,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vile, than the egg of the ostrich which it abandons</hi> (S, A, * K) <hi rend="ital">in the desert.</hi> (TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ بَيْضَةُ البَلَدِ</foreign> in dispraise and in praise. (IAar, Aboo-Bekr, M.) When said in dispraise, it means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He is like the egg of the ostrich from which the young bird has come forth, and which the male ostrich has cast away, so that men and camels tread upon it:</hi> (IAar, M:) or <hi rend="ital">he is alone, without any to aid him; like the egg from which the male ostrich has arisen, and which he has abandoned as useless:</hi> (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">he is an obscure man,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">one of no reputation, whose lineage is unknown.</hi> (Ham p. 250.) And when said in praise, it means <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He is like the ostrich's egg in which is the young bird;</hi> because the male ostrich in that case protects it: (IAar, M:) or <hi rend="ital">he is unequalled in nobility;</hi> like the egg that is left alone: (M:) or <hi rend="ital">he is a lord,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">chief:</hi> (IAar, M:) or <hi rend="ital">he is the unequalled of the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَلَد</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">country</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like</hi>], <hi rend="ital">to whom others resort, and whose words they accept:</hi> (K:) or <hi rend="ital">he is a celebrated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">wellknown, person.</hi> (Ham p. 250.) [See also art. <foreign lang="ar">بلد</foreign>. And for another meaning of <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَةُ البَلَدِ</foreign> see below.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">A helmet of iron,</hi> (AO, S, * M, * Mgh, * K, *) <hi rend="ital">which is composed of plates like the bones of the skull, the edges whereof are joined together by nails; and sometimes of one piece:</hi> (AO:) so called because resembling in shape the egg of an ostrich: (AO, M, Mgh: *) in this sense, also, n. un. of

(TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  The <hi rend="ital">bulb</hi> of the saffron-plant [&amp;c.]: as resembling an egg in shape.                   <hi rend="ital">Whiteness; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سَوَادٌ</foreign>; in an animal, and in a plant, and in other things; and, accord. to IAar, in water also; (M;) the colour of that which is termed <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضُ</foreign>: (S, Msb, * K:) they said <foreign lang="ar">بَيَاضٌ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3632-1" target="بَيَاضَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n3634"/></foreign>, (S, M, K,) like as they said <foreign lang="ar">مَنْزِلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَنْزِلَةٌ</foreign>: (S:) <foreign lang="ar">بَيَاضَةٌ</foreign> being applied to <hi rend="ital">a whiteness</hi> in the eye. (M.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا أَشَدُّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَيَاضًا مِنْ كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is whiter than such a thing</hi>]: (S, K: *) but not   
      <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضُ <ref cref="n3632-2" target="منْهُ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (S:) the latter is anomalous; (K;) [like <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ مِنْهُ</foreign>; q. v.;] but it was said by the people of El-Koofeh, (S, K,) who adduced as authority the saying of the rájiz, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">جَارِيَةٌ فِى دِرْعِهَا الفَضْفَاضِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضُ مِنْ أُخْتِ بَنِى إِبَاضِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">A damsel in her ample shift, whiter than the sister of</hi> the tribe of <hi rend="ital">Benoo-Ibád</hi>]: Mbr, however, says that an anomalous verse is no evidence against a rule commonly approved: and as to the saying of another, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا الرِّجَالُ شَتَوْا وَٱشْتَدَّ أَكْلُهُمُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">فَأَنْتَ أَبْيَضُهُمْ سِرْبَالَ طَبَّاخِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">When men experience dearth in winter, and their eating becomes vehement, thou art the whitest of them,</hi> or rather <hi rend="ital">the white of them, in respect of cook's clothing,</hi> having little or nothing to do with entertaining them], the word in question may be considered as an epithet of the measure <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعَلُ</foreign> that is followed by <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ</foreign> to denote excess: but it is only like the instances in the sayings <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ أَحْسَنُهُمْ وَجْهًا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَكْرَمُهُمْ أَبًا</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">حَسَنُهُمْ وَجْهًا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَرِيِمُهُمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَبًا</foreign>; so it is as though he said <foreign lang="ar">فَأَنْتَ مُبْيَضُّهُمْ سِرْبَالًا</foreign>; and as he has prefixed it to a complement which it governs in the gen. case, what follows is in the accus. case as a specificative. (S.) This latter verse is by Tarafeh, who satirizes therein 'Amr Ibn-Hind; and is also differently related in respect of the first hemistich, and the first word of the second.                   <hi rend="ital">White; contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَسْوَدُ</foreign>; (A, K;) <hi rend="ital">having whiteness:</hi> (Msb:) fem. <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَآءُ</foreign>: (Msb:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">بِيضٌ</foreign>, originally <foreign lang="ar">بُيْضٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) the damm being converted into kesr in order that the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> may remain unchanged, (S, K,) [i. e.] to suit the <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>. (Msb.) In the phrase <foreign lang="ar">أَعْطِنِى أَبْيَضَّهْ</foreign>, mentioned by Sb, as used by some of the Arabs, meaning <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضَ</foreign>, [i. e. <hi rend="ital">Give thou to me a white one,</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> is subjoined as it is in <foreign lang="ar">هُنَّهْ</foreign> for <foreign lang="ar">هُنَّ</foreign>, and the <foreign lang="ar">ض</foreign> is doubled because the letter of declinability cannot have <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> subjoined to it; wherefore the letter of declinability is the first <foreign lang="ar">ض</foreign>, and the second is the augmentative, and for this reason it has subjoined to it the <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> whereof the purpose is to render plainly perceivable the vowel [which is necessarily added after the doubled <foreign lang="ar">ض</foreign>]: Aboo-'Alee says, [app. of the <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign>,] that it should properly have neither fet-h nor any vowel. (M.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Applied to a man &amp;c., it was sometimes used to signify <hi rend="ital">White in complexion:</hi> but in this sense they generally used the epithet <foreign lang="ar">أَحْمَرُ</foreign>. (IAth, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">حمر</foreign>.) They also said, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ أَبْيَضُ الوَجْهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانَةُ بَيْضَآءُ الوَجْهِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Such a man,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">such a woman, is clear, in face, from freckles or the like, and unseemly blackness.</hi> (Az, TA.) And they used <foreign lang="ar">بِيضَانٌ</foreign>, (S, K,) a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضُ</foreign>, (TA,) in the contr. of the sense of <foreign lang="ar">سُودَانٌ</foreign>, (S, K,) [i. e. as signifying <hi rend="ital">Whites,</hi>] applied to men: (S:) though they applied the appellation <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو البَيْضَآءِ</foreign> to <hi rend="ital">the Abyssinian:</hi> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">عور</foreign>:) or to <hi rend="ital">the negro:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">أَبُو الجَوْنِ</foreign> to the white man. (ISk.) But accord. to Th, <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضُ</foreign> applied to a man signifies only <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Pure; free from faults:</hi> (IAth, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">حمر</foreign>:) or, so applied, <hi rend="ital">unsullied in honour, nobility,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">estimation;</hi> (Az, K;) <hi rend="ital">free from faults;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">generous:</hi> and so <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَآءُ</foreign> applied to a woman. (Az.) [In the lexicons, however, (see, for ex., among countless other instances, an explanation of <foreign lang="ar">بَضَّةٌ</foreign> in the S,) and in other post-classical works, it is generally used, when thus applied, in its proper sense, of <hi rend="ital">White;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fair in complexion.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَتِيبَةٌ بَيْضَآءُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">An army,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a portion thereof, upon which the whiteness of the</hi> [<hi rend="ital">arms or armour of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">iron is apparent.</hi> (M.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَآءُ</foreign> alone, [as a subst.,] <hi rend="ital">A piece of paper</hi> [<hi rend="ital">without writing</hi>]. (Har p. 311.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الأَبْيَضُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The sword:</hi> (S, A, K:) because of its whiteness: (TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">بِيضٌ</foreign>. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Silver:</hi> (A, K:) because of its whiteness: like as gold is called <foreign lang="ar">الأَحْمَرُ</foreign> [because of its redness]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">The saliva</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">رضاب</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">of the mouth.</hi> (Ham p. 348.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A certain star in the margin of the milky way.</hi> (A, K.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">البَيْضَآءُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The sun:</hi> because of its whiteness. (M.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Waste,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">uncultivated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">uninhabited, land:</hi> (K, * TA: [in the CK <foreign lang="ar">الجِرابُ</foreign> is erroneously put for <foreign lang="ar">الخَرَابُ</foreign>:]) opposed to <foreign lang="ar">السَّوْدَآءُ</foreign>: because dead lands are white; and when planted, become black and green. (TA.) See also <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَةٌ</foreign>, near the end.          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Wheat:</hi> (K:) as also <foreign lang="ar">السَّمْرَآءُ</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Fresh</hi> [<hi rend="ital">grain of the kind called</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">سُلْت</foreign>. (El- <pb n="284"/> Khattábee, K.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A certain kind of wood; that which is called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحَوَرُ</foreign>: (K in art. <foreign lang="ar">حور</foreign>:) because of its whiteness. (TA in that art.) [See <foreign lang="ar">حَوَرٌ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">The cooking-pot;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">أُمُّ بَيْضَآءَ</foreign>. (AA, K.)          <sense type="b" n="15">-b15-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">The snare with which one catches game.</hi> (IAar, K.)          <sense type="b" n="16">-b16-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الأَبْيَضَانِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Milk and water.</hi> (ISk, S, M, A, K.) A poet says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَمَا لِىَ إِلَّا الأَبْيَضَيْنِ شَرَابُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And I have not any beverage except milk and water</hi>]. (ISk, S, M.)          <sense type="b" n="17">-b17-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Bread and water:</hi> (As, M, K:) or <hi rend="ital">wheat and water:</hi> (Fr, K:) or <hi rend="ital">fat and milk.</hi> (AO, K.)          <sense type="b" n="18">-b18-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Fat and youthfulness</hi> (AZ, IAar, M, A, K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">ذَهَبَ أَبْيَضَاهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">His fat and youthfulness departed.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="19">-b19-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَا رَأَيْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مُذْ أَبْيَضَانِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I have not seen him for,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">during, two days:</hi> (Ks, M, A, K:) or <hi rend="ital">two months.</hi> (Ks, M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="20">-b20-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَيَّامُ البِيضِ</foreign>, (Msb, K,) or simply <foreign lang="ar">البِيضُ</foreign>, (Mgh,) for <foreign lang="ar">أَيَّامُ اللَّيَالِى البِيضِ</foreign>; [<hi rend="ital">The days of the white nights;</hi>] i. e. <hi rend="ital">the days of the thirteenth and fourteenth and fifteenth nights of the month;</hi> (Mgh, Msb, K;) so called because they are lighted by the moon throughout: (Msb:) or <hi rend="ital">of the twelfth and thirteenth and fourteenth nights:</hi> (K:) but this is of weak authority, and extr.: the former is the correct explanation: (MF, TA:) you should not say <foreign lang="ar">الأَيَّامُ البِيضُ</foreign>: (Ibn-El-Jawá- leekee, IB, K:) yet thus it is in most relations of a trad. in which it occurs; and some argue for it; and the author of the K has himself explained <foreign lang="ar">الأَوَاضِحُ</foreign> by <foreign lang="ar">الأَيَّامُ البِيضُ</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="21">-b21-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سَنَةٌ بَيْضَآءُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A year</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of scarcity of herbage,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">such as is a mean between that which is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَهْبَآء</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">and that which is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَمْرَآء</foreign>. (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">شهب</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="22">-b22-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَلَامٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَبْيَضُ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Language expounded</hi> or <hi rend="ital">explained.</hi> (M.)          <sense type="b" n="23">-b23-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَلَّمْتُهُ فَمَا رَدَّ عَلَىَّ سَوْدَآءَ وَلَا بَيْضَآءَ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">I spoke to him, and he did not return to me a bad word nor a good one.</hi> (M.)          <sense type="b" n="24">-b24-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">يَدٌ بَيْضَآءُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A demonstrating,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">demonstrated, argument, plea, allegation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">evidence.</hi> (M.)          <sense type="b" n="25">-b25-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A favour,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">benefit, for which one is not reproached;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">which is conferred without its being asked.</hi> (M.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">يَدٌ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="26">-b26-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">المَوْتُ الأَبْيَضُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Sudden death;</hi> (K, TA;) <hi rend="ital">such as is not preceded by disease which alters the complexion:</hi> or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">death without the repentance, and the prayer for forgiveness, and the accomplishment of necessary duties, usual with him who is not taken unawares;</hi> from <foreign lang="ar">بَيَّضَ</foreign> signifying “ he emptied ” a vessel: so says Sgh: opposed to <foreign lang="ar">المَوْتُ الأَحْمَرُ</foreign>, which is slaughter. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="27">-b27-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَآءُ</foreign> also signifies <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">A calamity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">misfortune:</hi> (Sgh, K:) app. as a term of good omen; like <foreign lang="ar">سَلِيمٌ</foreign> applied to one who is stung by a scorpion or bitten by a serpent. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="28">-b28-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَآءُ القَيْظِ</foreign>: see <foreign lang="ar">بَيْضَةٌ</foreign>, last sentence but one.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا أَبْيَضُ مِنْ كَذَا</foreign>; &amp;c.: see <foreign lang="ar">بَيَاضٌ</foreign>.    </entryFree>2c:T46c,<entryFree id="n3641" key="مُبَيِّضٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مُبَيِّضٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">مبيض</orth>
                  </form> A man <hi rend="ital">wearing white clothing.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Hence, <foreign lang="ar">المُبَيِّضَةُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A sect of</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the class called</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ثَنَوِيَّة</foreign>, (S, K,) the companions of <foreign lang="ar">المُقَنَّع</foreign>; (S;) <hi rend="ital">so called because they made their clothes white, in contradistinction to the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مُسَوِّدَة</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">the partisans of the dynasty of the 'Abbásees;</hi> (S, K, *) <hi rend="ital">for the distinction of these was black: they dwelt in Kasr 'Omeyr.</hi> (TA.)
